**The Precepts of Hook and Reckoning, The Three Lights and Five Precepts of the Ancient Teachings, The Precepts of the Five Brightnesses, The Precepts of the Spirit’s Salvation, The Precepts of the Yin’s Natural Assistance, The Precepts of Riding the Dragon and Driving the Clouds, The Diagram of the Eastern Wall, The Diagram of the Western Wall, The Self-Sequence of the Divine Person, The *Xing Shang* Precepts, The *Xing Shang* Precepts of Virtue and Conduct, The *Xing Shang* Precepts of the Spirit’s Assistance**

**The Daoist Precepts of the Taiping Section — External Category** **[Nine scrolls]** — *The Taiping Jing: Sacred Ruler’s Secret Guard*
**The Precepts of the Ten Exalted Conditions, The Precepts of the Great Sage’s Upper Chapter, The Precepts of Knowing the Ghostly and the Revered, The Precepts of Long Virtue and Blessing, The Precepts of the Heavenly Lord’s Decree for Merit, etc.**
*All the above are categorized within the Taiping Jing, which was originally divided into sections by the Eight Trigrams (甲乙丙丁戊己庚辛壬癸). Each section contains seventeen scrolls, totaling one hundred and fifty scrolls. All teachings focus on cultivating the body, nurturing the nature, preserving the essence, and loving the spirit. Internally, they promote bodily refinement and longevity; externally, they advocate governance, peace, disaster mitigation, and disease treatment—all proven effective.*

---

---
...The *Taiping Jing* (Sacred Ruler’s Secret Guard) is calculated by the *Fangzi* (奉字) numbering to nine scrolls.

The *Taiping Jing* (Sacred Ruler’s Secret Guard) also includes:
**The *Lingbao Jing* (Scripture of Numinous Treasure) – *Zhengming Dongshen Shangpin Jing* (Pure Clarity Cavernous Spirit Supreme Grade Scripture) [2 scrolls]**
*Upper scroll, seventeen chapters: on cultivating the True Dao (修真) in ranks, the marvelous existence of treasured diagrams (妙有宝图).*
*Lower scroll, thirty-five chapters: on wearing talismans (佩服), treasured diagrams (宝箓), and methods of pacification (安镇), invocation (呼召), etc.*

**The *Lingbao Zhengming Yuzhen Shuzhen Jing* (Scripture of the Pure Clarity Dao’s True Axis and Pivot) [Transmitted by the *Xiandu Jun* (仙都君)]**

**The *Lingbao Zhengming Dao Yuan Yuyin Jing* (Scripture of the Pure Clarity Dao’s Origin and Jade Seal) [The following four lines constitute the *Zhengming Xin Yin* (Pure Clarity Heart Seal):*
*"In the boundless void, the mind is tranquil and clear;
The inner and outer realms are illuminated;
No entanglement with things—this is the Dao’s essence.
These four sentences are the Pure Clarity Heart Seal."]

**The *Lingbao Zhengming Tianzun Shuo Yuwen Jing* (Heavenly Sovereign’s Scripture on Ruling the Plague) [Contains talismans (符)]**

**The *Lingbao Shouru Zhengming Siguijian Jing* (Scripture of the Pure Clarity Dao’s Four Rules and Clear Mirror) [Same scroll as the *Shuzhen* Four Scriptures]**

**The *Lingbao Zhengming Jiuxian Shui Jing* (Scripture of the Pure Clarity Dao’s Nine Immortals’ Water) [Contains diagrams (图)]**
*"To nourish life, let the *qi* circulate through the four limbs;
Then the blood’s pathways flow and permeate the body—
Guard the five *zang* organs (五脏) in their origins and destinations,
And you shall know the River of Heaven (河通天) and Heaven’s Communication with the Sea (天通海).
The Sea guards Kunlun (昆仑), and the Yellow River flows in reverse—thus the Dao is sealed."*

**The *Lingbao Zhengming Zhonghuang Bajiu Jing* (Scripture of the Pure Clarity Dao’s Central Yellow Eight Pillars) [Same scroll as the *Jiuxian Shui Jing*]**
*"The Central Yellow’s Dao (中黄之道) is the vision of the Yellow Court (黄庭之景);
The four *gu* valleys (虚四谷) are sealed, the two *dui* (二兑) are guarded,
And the two *dong* (洞) are fortified—
Establish the eight pillars (立八柱),
Rectify the true position (正位), rectify the true nature (正性),
And merge the essence and life (混含性命).
This is the true method for attaining the Dao."*

**The *Zhengming Zhongxiao Quan Shu* (Complete Book of Pure Clarity Loyalty and Filial Piety) [Scrolls 1 to 6, totaling five scrolls]**
*Compiled by the Pure Clarity Dao’s Teaching Master, Huang Yuangji (黄元吉).*
*"Pure Clarity Dao (浄明) is simply rectifying the heart and sincerity of intent;
Loyalty and filial piety (忠孝) are merely upholding the fundamental principles (纲常).
Yet many students, though familiar with these words, recite them mechanically without understanding—
They neglect the essence and instead focus on true practice, diligent cultivation (工夫),
And only then shall they align with the four characters (四字).
The truly loyal (大忠) deceive nothing,
The truly filial (大孝) love all beings.
The truly pure (浄) defile nothing,
The truly clear (明) touch nothing—
No defilement, no attachment.
Loyalty and filial piety are naturally attained.
It is also said:
'Loyalty is loyalty to the ruler (忠者忠于君也);
The heart is the ruler—
The ruler is the sovereign of all the *shen* (神).
A single thought of deceit is disloyalty.'"*

The *Muzi* (母字) numbering is calculated to ten scrolls.

They emphasize moral instruction through language, awakening those lost in confusion. Even more, his life of cold detachment embodies the true Immortal’s style, and his words carry no trace of mundane sentimentality. Those who merely recite poems of wind and moon without practical meaning are speaking empty words.*]

**The *Chóngyáng* Ten Transformations from Dividing the Pear Collection** [*Upper and Lower, 2 Scrolls*]
[*This collection stems from Chongyáng Zhēnrén of Zhōngnán Mountain residing in Dànyáng at the Mǎ Zìrán household, where he took up abode as their teacher. Chongyáng Zhēnrén wished for the couple to swiftly cultivate and abandon their familial ties, severing their roots to become wandering Daoists. Initially, they agreed easily. Chongyáng Zhēnrén then vowed to fast in the hermitage for a hundred days, beginning from the first auspicious day of the second month of winter. The imperial decree granted him the title of "Dividing the Pear," and he would offer them a pear every ten days, starting from two pieces and increasing to fifty. Every five days, he also bestowed six yams or chestnuts, along with vivid dreams depicting the Ten Offenses of Heavenly and Hellish Precepts, stirring their resolve. Each time he gave them a pear, he composed poems or songs, subtly warning them. The couple responded in kind, fulfilling the celestial union of yin and yang’s wondrous pairing. Through this, they understood the mechanisms of calamity and fortune, life and death, and thus abandoned worldly entanglements, reformed their attire, and burned their oaths. The couple turned to him in faith as their teacher. This collection gathers over three hundred poems and songs, all on profound Daoist principles, hence the name "Ten Transformations from Dividing the Pear."*]]

**The *Chóngyáng* Golden Key and Jade Lock Method** [*The Chongyáng Zǐ of Zhōngnán Mountain’s collection, on the gradual cultivation of the True Dao.*]

**The *Chángchūn* Zǐ Mǎnxī Collection** [*Scroll 1 of 6, the Qīxiá Chángchūn Zǐ Qiū Chǔjī’s collection, containing poems, songs, and melodies. Each phrase and word serves to awaken the deaf and blind, washing away the dust of mundane distractions.*]
**The *Tán* Master’s *Shuǐyún* Collection** [*3 Scrolls, the Kunlun Mountain Chángzhēn Zǐ Tán Chǔduān’s collection of poems, hymns, and essays, numbering only a few hundred. It includes songs about bones and destitution, warning and awakening the world. All writings contain profound Daoist applications, elucidating the true wind and guiding people toward goodness. They are greatly beneficial to the world.*]

**The *Tóu*-numbered Series: Seven Scrolls**
**The *Sūn* Master’s *Qiānjīn* Prescriptions Catalog** [*2 Scrolls*]
[*This catalog encompasses discussions on the viscera and bowels, acupuncture and moxibustion methods, pulse and symptom differentiation, dietary therapies, and the treatment of women, infants, leg qi, stroke, colds, abscesses, diabetes, edema, and ailments of the seven orifices. It also covers the five poisonous stones and emergency prescriptions, life-nourishing techniques, totaling 232 entries and 5,300 prescriptions. All are complete and verifiable, encompassing four types of methods. The Master’s legacy surpasses the value of a thousand gold pieces, and his prescriptions endure for generations.*]

[*The Master’s given name was Sīmiào, a native of Huáyuán, Jīngzhào. At seven, he began his studies, reciting ten thousand words daily. Later, he secluded himself in Tàishān to study the Dao, attaining mastery and perfecting his knowledge of medicine. Once, he treated the Dragon Prince and obtained thirty prescriptions from the Dragon Palace, all of which proved miraculously effective when tested. He then compiled the *Qiānjīn* Prescriptions in one hundred scrolls, preserving the Dragon Palace formulas within.*]

He discussed the principles and distinctions of punishment and virtue. Though the scrolls are incomplete, his school’s essence remains evident.*]

**The Huainan Hongle Commentary** [*Scroll 15 of 23*]

**The Pí-Character Series: Eight Scrolls**
**The Huainan Hongle Commentary** [*Scroll 24 of 28*]
[*King An of Huainan was the eldest son of King Huli of Chu. This text aligns closely with the Supreme Daoist Lord Lao’s teachings of detachment and non-action, of following the void and maintaining stillness, of entering and exiting the Dao. In its grandeur, it encompasses the celestial and terrestrial; in its subtlety, it descends into the boundless. It records the rise and fall of ancient and modern governance, the survival and perishing of states, the calamities and blessings of the world, and the intricate, wondrous, and strange affairs of humanity. Its meanings are profound, its words rich, and its scope exhaustive, yet its essence is ultimately rooted in the Dao, hence the name "Hongle Commentary."*]

**The Inner Chapters of the Master Bàopǔ** [*Scroll 1 of 6*]
**The Shǒu-Character Series: Eleven Scrolls**
**The Inner Chapters of the Master Bàopǔ** [*Scroll 7 of 20*]
[*The Inner Chapters expound the Dao of immortality, contrasting it with the mundane. They delve into the profound principles of alchemy and elixirs, elucidating the essence of the Dao, clarifying the nature of elixirs, and meticulously addressing questions on diligent cultivation, the interplay of yellow and white (alchemy), the exploration of the earthly and the true, and strange transformations. They also include treatises on exorcising spirits and more. The twenty chapters all pertain to Daoist practices of elixir cultivation, life-nurturing, longevity, warding off malevolence, and averting calamities.*]

**The Master Bàopǔ’s Separate Treatise on Protection** [*Same Scroll as the Inner Chapters*]
**The Zhēn-Character Series: Twelve Scrolls**
**The Outer Chapters of the Master Bàopǔ** [*Scroll 1 of 37*]
**The Zhì-Character Series: Twelve Scrolls**
**The Outer Chapters of the Master Bàopǔ** [*Scroll 38 of 50*]
[*The Outer Chapters discuss virtuous withdrawal, reclusive scholars, encouraging learning, aligning with the Dao, upholding proper governance, ministerial loyalty, and rectifying the times. They address the selection and appointment of officials, the proper use of punishment, and the rectification of names. They also include critiques on litigation, warnings against excess, censures of misguided beliefs, and satirical attacks on arrogance. Additionally, they cover topics like the Hundred Li of the world, fishing for the world’s affairs, avoiding troubles, valuing breadth of knowledge, surpassing the Wu School, losing the Dao, and the principles of poverty and virtue. The language is rich in metaphors and analogies, yet its meaning remains rooted in the Dao, encompassing and surpassing all other schools. It also includes treatises on rectifying the Guanzheng School, refuting false claims, questioning errors, understanding cessation and exhaustion, and the Master’s self-introduction. The fifty scrolls discuss human affairs, gains and losses, and the Daoist perspective on the world, belonging to the Confucian tradition.*]

[*Discusses the principles of Heavenly Dao, yin and yang, the Five Phases, the Eight Trigrams, and the waxing and waning of celestial forces.*]

**The Secretly Transmitted Scripture of the True and Auspicious Lord of the Soul’s Treasure and Supreme Method** [*Three Scrolls, expounded by Cloud Room True Person, Zhongli Quan*]
[*Discusses the Dao of Heavenly Dao, yin and yang, the elevation and descent of the cosmos, the waxing and waning of celestial phases, and the interplay of their conjunctions. It elucidates the principle of *qi* generating water and water generating *qi*, the exchange between heart and kidneys, and the pairing of celestial stems and earthly branches (Jia-Yi and Geng-Xu). It further explains the distinction between pure and impure water sources, the recognition of internal landscapes, and the cultivation of the Dao through elixir refinement and life-nurturing. This Scripture is a profound and hidden text.*]
